                         {
                              "title": "disable logging worker exceptions to the console",
                              "description": "The current worker handler logs exceptions to the console. Given that exception transfer between the worker and the client is really smooth, I think many folks would want to leverage it, but may not want to dump dirty laundry on the console.\r\n```js\r\n            function registerPromiseWorker(callback) {\r\n                function postOutgoingMessage(e, messageId, error, result) {\r\n                    if (error) {\r\n                        if (typeof console !== 'undefined' && 'error'in console) {\r\n                            // This is to make errors easier to debug. I think it's important\r\n                            // enough to just leave here without giving the user an option\r\n                            // to silence it.\r\n                            console.error('Worker caught an error:', error)\r\n                        }\r\n```\r\nA switch would allow workers to debug by default but turn it off if they don't want it.",
                              "label": "unlabeledBug",
                              "createdAt": "2020-09-29T14:21:23Z",

                         {
                              "title": "Send error stack traces to the main thread",
                              "description": "The README currently says:\r\n\r\n> Note that stacktraces cannot be sent from the worker to the main thread\r\n\r\nI'm guessing you wrote that because listening to `Worker.onerror` gets an `ErrorEvent` object, but the `error` property is always null for some reason, and because you can't send error objects over `postMessage`.\r\n\r\nHowever in the worker (either via try/catch of `self.onerror`), you can see the stack trace. And `Error.stack` is just a string, so even though you can't send the actual `Error` back via `self.postMessage`, you can send the stack.\r\n\r\nThis requires some extra complexity, because you need to distinguish between different types of messages sent from promise-worker itself, similar to the \"multi-type messages\" example in the README, but working internally.\r\n\r\nEven better, you can send all the properties of the error back, and then assign them all to a new error object in the main thread. Then it is nearly transparent to the user, it seems as if the real error object has been transferred. Except... if you use source maps, they won't work. You can still use source maps manually, of course. And even better, third-party error tracking services like https://www.bugsnag.com/ are smart enough to apply the source maps to your \"fake\" error objects automatically!\r\n\r\nAll of this is implemented in [my fork of this project](https://github.com/dumbmatter/promise-worker-bi/). I'm unlikely to send a PR here because I don't know if you want the additional message-passing complexity, and because my fork has substantially diverged from yours at this point. But I figured I'd leave a note here in case any users were wondering about error handling.",

                              "title": "Redundant unhandledrejection events",
                              "description": "Hi,\r\n\r\nif you'll write something like this:\r\n\r\n```js\r\nPromise.reject('reject')\r\n  .finally(() => console.warn('finally'))\r\n  .catch(() => console.warn('catch'));\r\n```\r\n\r\nYou'll get the following output:\r\n\r\n```\r\nfinally\r\ncatch\r\nPromise {[[PromiseStatus]]: \"resolved\", [[PromiseValue]]: undefined}\r\nUncaught (in promise) reject\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe last `Uncaught (in promise) reject` looks to be odd here, because the promise was properly handled.\r\n\r\nHere is another example, where the promise rejection was not handled:\r\n\r\n```js\r\nPromise.reject('reject')\r\n  .finally(() => console.warn('finally'));\r\n```\r\n\r\nand the output is:\r\n\r\n```\r\nfinally\r\nPromise {[[PromiseStatus]]: \"rejected\", [[PromiseValue]]: \"reject\"}\r\nUncaught (in promise) reject\r\nUncaught (in promise) reject\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe promise rejection was not handled at all and we got two `unhandledrejection` instead of one.\r\n\r\nEach new `finally` in promise chain will produce one extra `unhandledrejection` event. This will result in four events triggered:\r\n\r\n```js\r\nPromise.reject('reject')\r\n  .finally(() => console.warn('finally'))\r\n  .finally(() => console.warn('finally'))\r\n  .finally(() => console.warn('finally'));\r\n```\r\n\r\nDoes this correct behaviour? If yes, then how should I handle those extra rejections?",

                         {
                              "title": "shim() not shimming on karma/phantomJS",
                              "description": "For some weird reason the shim() isn't able to shim the global Promise on karma with the phantomJS driver (the main app works fine, and the jasmine client version of the specs work fine on other browsers).\r\n\r\nWhen debugging I see the shim hitting define-property here:\r\n```js\r\nif (supportsDescriptors) {\r\n // it actually fires this\r\n  Object.defineProperty(object, name, {\r\n    configurable: true,\r\n    enumerable: false,\r\n    value: value,\r\n    writable: true\r\n  });\r\n} else { ... }\r\n```\r\nbut then\r\n```js\r\nrequire('promise.prototype.finally').shim()\r\nconsole.log(Promise.prototype.finally) // logs undefined\r\n``` \r\n\r\nNow if I pass the Promise object to the shim and change the library function signature accordingly it works\r\n```js\r\n// shim.js\r\n...\r\nmodule.exports = function shimPromiseFinally(obj) {\r\n\tobj = obj || Promise;\r\n\trequirePromise();\r\n\r\n\tvar polyfill = getPolyfill();\r\n\tdefine(obj.prototype, { 'finally': polyfill }, {\r\n\t\t'finally': function testFinally() {\r\n\t\t\treturn obj.prototype['finally'] !== polyfill;\r\n\t\t}\r\n\t});\r\n\treturn polyfill;\r\n};\r\n...\r\n\r\n\r\n// karma.entry.js\r\nrequire('promise.prototype.finally').shim(Promise)\r\nconsole.log(Promise.prototype.finally) // logs the polyfill, it works!\r\n```\r\n\r\nI can submit a PR if you think this is something you want to add (I've seen other shimming libs do this too, perhaps this is a common issue)\r\n\r\n-----\r\nPS: for anyone wondering this is my quick fix for now:\r\n```js\r\nconst finallyPolyfill = require('promise.prototype.finally').shim()\r\n\r\n// Make sure we're shimming promise.finally.\r\n// (auto .shim() doesn't work in karma for some reason)\r\nif (!Promise.prototype.finally) { Promise.prototype.finally = finallyPolyfill }\r\n```",

                              "title": "Prototype Inheritance (Tiny Emitter)",
                              "description": "#### Bug Description\r\nIf the `eventName` is in the set of properties defined in Object.prototype (`constructor`, `hasOwnProperty`, `isPrototypeOf`, `propertyIsEnumerable`, `toLocaleString`, `toString`, `valueOf`), there would be a TypeError on [this line](https://github.com/kwolfy/webworker-promise/blob/366eeb8a805745b82cb17a047df4ef69cd4f5b9d/src/tiny-emitter.js#L34).\r\n\r\nThis happens because, in JavaScript, objects inherit from Object.prototype by default. This can create potential issues that, although may be unlikely to happen, still represent a risk. \r\n\r\n#### Fix \r\nOne of the possible fixes for this is creating the object without enabling prototype inheritance. More specifically, this would affect the `__listeners` property defined in `TinyEmitter`. Applying the fix suggested below makes the application not to crash even if the `eventName` is a string in the set of properties listed above.\r\n\r\n--- TinyEmitter constructor (original) ---\r\n```\r\nclass TinyEmitter {\r\n  constructor() {\r\n    Object.defineProperty(this, '__listeners', {\r\n      value: {},\r\n      ...\r\n    });\r\n  }\r\n...\r\n}\r\n```\r\n\r\n--- Tiny Emitter constructor (fixed) ---\r\n```\r\nclass TinyEmitter {\r\n  constructor() {\r\n    Object.defineProperty(this, '__listeners', {\r\n      value: Object.create(null),\r\n      ...\r\n    });\r\n  }\r\n...\r\n}\r\n```",

                         {
                              "title": "Promise is being rejected given message with value `null`",
                              "description": "The promise returned by `postMessage` seems to be rejected given a message with value`null`. I would expect the promise to be resolved, as the [`postMessage` API](https://html.spec.whatwg.org/multipage/web-messaging.html#dom-messageport-postmessage) allows sending messages with value `null`. \r\n\r\n### How to reproduce the issue?\r\nI wrote a simple client of the library, which imports `WebworkerPromise` and posts a message with `null` value. The worker handler does nothing except returning the message received from the `main` thread. The promise is then rejected and we get an error in the `main` thread, captured with the `catch` clause.\r\n\r\n**main.js**\r\n```\r\nconst WebworkerPromise = require('webworker-promise');\r\nconst worker = new WebworkerPromise(new Worker('worker.js'));\r\n\r\nworker\r\n  .postMessage(null)\r\n  .then((response) => {\r\n  \tconsole.log('MAIN: got response '+response);\r\n    // handle response\r\n  })\r\n  .catch(error => {\r\n  \tconsole.log('MAIN: got error '+error);\r\n    // handle error\r\n  });\r\n```\r\n\r\n**worker.js**\r\n```\r\nconst registerWebworker = require('webworker-promise/lib/register');\r\n\r\nregisterWebworker(\r\n  (message, emit) => {\r\n    return message;\r\n  }\r\n);\r\n```\r\n\r\n### How to fix?\r\nThe error originates in the function below, taken from **register.js**. When `o` has value `null` (which is exactly the case of the example shown above), we cannot access the `then` property without checking if `o` has value `null`. \r\n```\r\nconst isPromise = o => typeof o === 'object' && typeof o.then === 'function' && typeof o.catch === 'function';\r\n```\r\nThus, checking if `o` is null before accessing the `then` property would solve the issue and avoid the promise to be rejected. We could then have the following instead:\r\n```\r\nconst isPromise = o => typeof o === 'object' && o !== null && typeof o.then === 'function' && typeof o.catch === 'function';\r\n```",

                         {
                              "title": "\"resolve\" method is broken",
                              "description": "This is kind of weird bug report because I found the problem not by running your code, but by doing a verbatim translation into Emacs Lisp, because it I wanted to implement promises and your code was the simplest implementation I could find to use as a model. It appears it was a little _too_ simple, because the equivalent of this code failed to work:\r\n\r\n`Promise.resolve(42).then(x => Promise.resolve(x + 1)).then(y => assert(y == 43));`\r\n\r\nThe problem is that `y` is a promise rather than a number. I discovered a simple fix by looking at Google's implementation, which adds a 4th state, `BLOCKED`. When a promise is resolved with another promise (`promise.js` [line 92](https://github.com/bramstein/promis/blob/b2a87519fba6a445638c6b6616ebbfbf164e408e/src/promise.js#L92) in your code), the promise should go into the `BLOCKED`  state, and stay in that state until lines 95, 101, and 109, where it should be put back into the pending state just before the call to `resolve` or `reject`. Finally, the `notify` method needs to treat `BLOCKED` as equivalent to `PENDING`. I haven't tested the fix in your code, but it works in mine.\r\n\r\n(BTW, I think it's worth updating your code, because it's still the best model I could find for a new implementation of promises. Google's version is well tested and full of bells and whistles, but also far more complex and full of questionable optimizations that obscure the basic logic.)",

                              "title": "\"#<Object> is not a constructor\" when used with TypeScript's `allowSyntheticDefaultImports` & `esModuleInterop`",
                              "description": "I'm hitting trouble when trying to use this library in a TypeScript & Babel project. I installed both the lib and the types as usual:\r\n\r\n```\r\nnpm i promise.allsettled @types/promise.allsettled\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe standard `require` (as described in README) is not TypeScript-friendly, which is normal:\r\n\r\n```ts\r\nconst allSettled = require('promise.allsettled');\r\n\r\n// allSettled is `any` at this point, @types are unused\r\n```\r\n\r\nThat's why the [type tests](https://github.com/DefinitelyTyped/DefinitelyTyped/blob/1d3c2241784d39d9378c99473f629cb77f5c8e89/types/promise.allsettled/promise.allsettled-tests.ts#L1) use this syntax:\r\n\r\n```ts\r\nimport allSettled = require(\"promise.allsettled\");\r\n```\r\n\r\nHowever, that's not supported by Babel 7 and transitively by all tools that depend on it. For example, our Jest tests fail with this:\r\n\r\n> SyntaxError: demo.ts: `import =` is not supported by @babel/plugin-transform-typescript\r\n    Please consider using `import <moduleName> from '<moduleName>';` alongside Typescript's --allowSyntheticDefaultImports option.\r\n    \r\nAgain, this is quite normal and the common fix is to create this `tsconfig.json`:\r\n\r\n```json\r\n{\r\n  \"compilerOptions\": {\r\n    \"allowSyntheticDefaultImports\": true,\r\n    \"esModuleInterop\": true,\r\n  }\r\n}\r\n```\r\n\r\nand use this import syntax:\r\n\r\n```ts\r\nimport allSettled from 'promise.allsettled';\r\n```\r\n\r\nWe use this for several other modules and even with `promise.allsettled`, TypeScript is happy at this point and Jest test pass (the `promise.allsettled` code is executed correctly at runtime!).\r\n\r\n_However_, it leads to this error when running the app through plain `node` (or via `ts-node`):\r\n\r\n```\r\nTypeError: #<Object> is not a constructor\r\n    at Object.resolve (<anonymous>)\r\n    at Object.PromiseResolve (/example/node_modules/promise.allsettled/node_modules/es-abstract/es2018.js:160:10)\r\n    at /example/node_modules/promise.allsettled/implementation.js:26:24\r\n    at Function.from (<anonymous>)\r\n    at Object.allSettled (/example/node_modules/promise.allsettled/implementation.js:19:22)\r\n    at Object.allSettled [as default] (/example/node_modules/promise.allsettled/index.js:16:9)\r\n    at myFunction (/example/demo.ts:329:53)\r\n    at process._tickCallback (internal/process/next_tick.js:68:7)\r\n```\r\n\r\nMy theory is this: in the `--esModuleInterop` & `allowSyntheticDefaultImports` mode,  TypeScript transpiles the import to this:\r\n\r\n```js\r\n\"use strict\";\r\nvar __importDefault = (this && this.__importDefault) || function (mod) {\r\n    return (mod && mod.__esModule) ? mod : { \"default\": mod };\r\n};\r\nObject.defineProperty(exports, \"__esModule\", { value: true });\r\nconst promise_allsettled_1 = __importDefault(require(\"promise.allsettled\"));\r\n```\r\n\r\nNote how it wrapped the module into `default` property, so the usages look like this in the transpiled code:\r\n\r\n```js\r\nawait promise_allsettled_1.default(...)\r\n```\r\n\r\nAnd probably, `promise.allsettled` doesn't like this and throws the `#<Object> is not a constructor` error.\r\n\r\nI didn't dive deep into how the various \"binds\" in this library work but if there was a way to make it more friendly to that specific TypeScript emit scenario, that would be great.",

                         {
                              "title": "request: ability to disable prefetch",
                              "description": "Thanks for this library!\r\n\r\nI am using this library in an AWS Lambda, and ran into an interesting bug caused by the prefetch behavior. My app has code that looks like this:\r\n```\r\nasync function doGetCredentials() {\r\n  // ...async retrieval of credentials that expire after 1 hour...\r\n  return credentials;\r\n}\r\n\r\n// memoize credentials while they are valid\r\nconst getCredentials = promiseMemoize(doGetCredentials, { maxAge: credentialExpiryAge } );\r\n\r\ngetCredentials().then(doStuff).then(returnResponse);\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe issue I encountered is that AWS Lambdas can be immediately paused (i.e. JS execution stops) as soon as a response is returned, and then re-animated later to handle future requests. This can lead to a scenario where:\r\n1) request comes in, `doGetCredentials` is called and the result is memoized\r\n1) another request comes when the memoized result is \"almost expired\", so the prefetch request is triggered, but the memoized value is returned.\r\n1) my code returns a response without waiting for the prefetch request to complete, so Lambda execution is frozen. This happens after the credential request has been made, but before the doGetCredentials promise is fully resolved (i.e. before the refreshed value is memoized). \r\n1) another request comes in some time later, so Lambda execution resumes. finally the prefetch promise resolves, and the result is cached for `maxAge`. But the credentials being saved are from some time ago, so they could be already expired (or almost expired). Subsequent requests can get expired credentials.\r\n\r\nI think the cleanest fix to this problem would be to just disable the prefetching behavior, so that my response always waits for the credential request to complete, and Lambda can't pause execution mid-way through the credential request.",

                         {
                              "title": "No standard way to cancel promises / async operations",
                              "description": "And also no reasonable way to implement it in userland.\r\n\r\nFor instance, one can override native promises with [Bluebird](http://bluebirdjs.com) promises which expose an optional cancellation API, **_but_** this API does not inter-operate with modern async constructs such as async functions, generators and iterators.\r\n\r\nIMO, this (not to mention the forgoing of native promises altogether for cancellation's sake) is a price too high to pay in the long run.\r\n\r\n## Suggestion\r\n\r\nWithout forcing the community to agree on a \"right\" way to implement cancellations, _hooks_ can be provided to allow developers a way to standardize cancellations in their respective applications and in the way they see fit.\r\n\r\n[This reference implementation](https://gist.github.com/itaysabato/f78394793ae265c7895e862c2b2bd215) demonstrates a possible implementation of a \"Bluebird-style\" cancellation API on top of native promises via a promise _interception_ hooks API that I drafted therein.\r\n\r\nBoth the implementation and the suggested interception API should be considered as a _proof of concept_ that may be incomplete and possibly buggy.\r\n\r\n## Additional use cases\r\n\r\nThese kinds of interception hooks could prove useful for implementing additional use cases, e.g. for debugging tools etc.\r\n\r\nI will add these additional use cases as separate issues that will reference this one.",

                              "title": "from/to states passed in should not be mutated",
                              "description": "Problem: \n\n```\nimport animate from 'gsap-promise';\n\nconst from = {opacity: 0};\nconst to = {opacity: 1};\n\nPromise.all([\n    animate.fromTo(el1, 0.5, from, to),\n    animate.fromTo(el2, 0.5, from, to),\n])\n\n```\n\nThe first promise never resolves because the onComplete is overwritten by the second call\n\nThis would be solved if the object is shallow cloned before having options added on by the library\n#### Current workaround\n\nDefensively clone everything passed into gsap-promise\n\n```\nPromise.all([\n    animate.fromTo(el1, 0.5, {...from}, {...to}),\n    animate.fromTo(el2, 0.5, {...from}, {...to}),\n])\n```\n",

                              "title": "Functions missing environment variables because they are not found in cloud Formation",
                              "description": "## Exact error produced in the CLI Log\r\n\r\n> Serverless: [serverless-resources-env] WARNING: Could not find cloud formation resources for addPartner.Could not find: [List of resources missing]\r\n\r\n## Problem\r\nIf you have a stack that involves more then 100 resources (not hard to do) this plugin will fail to grab some of those resources when it makes the request to Amazon.  It is using the describe-stack-resources command that is limited to the first 100 resources in the stack.\r\n\r\n## Code where the problem exists\r\n_index.js_\r\n ```\r\n /**\r\n   * Looks up the CF Resources for this stack from AWS\r\n   * @returns {Promise.<String>}\r\n   */\r\n  fetchCFResources() {\r\n    const stackName = this.getStackName();\r\n    this.serverless.cli.log(`[serverless-resources-env] Looking up resources for CF Named: ${stackName}`);\r\n    return Promise.promisify(this.cloudFormation.describeStackResources.bind(this.cloudFormation))({\r\n      StackName: stackName,\r\n    });\r\n  }\r\n```\r\n## Fix\r\nPlease update this to instead use the **list-stack-resources** function provided by AWS. By default it uses pagination.  I believe there is an option to not paginate if that is easier.  \r\n\r\nI would totally update it and make a pull request but javascript is definitely not in my wheelhouse for now.  Doesn't mean I'm not going to try, but I don't have all that much time to spend on it.\r\n\r\n## Appreciation\r\nI really do appreciate that you took the time to make this plugin.  It really allows me to create a very dynamic application and deploy it at whim without having to worry about all the resources new id's/keys.  I would really like to see this fixed. This is the only fault I've seen so far.\r\n\r\n#### Bribery\r\nSays you're from the Long Beach, CA in your profile. I call the LBC home too.  Fix and deploy and I'll buy you a beer! 🍺 \r\n",

])\r\n} catch (err: any) {\r\n    console.log(err)\r\n    throw new Error(err);\r\n}\r\n``` \r\n\r\nand I get the following Error output:\r\n```\r\nethereum-sourcify: TypeError: #<Object> is not a                               "description": "Hi there, first off thanks for throwing this together -- it has been quite handy for the project I am currently working on.\r\n\r\nI noticed some unexpected behaviour / perhaps a bug -- it seems that while you can have helpers that return async values and the template will render correctly, async values in the context are hit and miss.  For example, this works:\r\n\r\n```js\r\nconst ctx = { somePromisedValue: Promise.resolve('yup') };\r\nconst template = handlebarsWithAsync.compile('{{ somePromisedValue }}');\r\nconsole.log(await template(ctx));\r\n// output = yup\r\n```\r\n\r\nHowever, if I try and make use of [nesting](https://handlebarsjs.com/guide/#nested-input-objects):\r\n\r\n```js\r\nconst ctx = { somePromisedValue: Promise.resolve({ v: 'yup' }) };\r\nconst template = handlebarsWithAsync.compile('{{ somePromisedValue.v }}');\r\nconsole.log(await template(ctx));\r\n// output = \r\n```\r\n\r\nIt looks like this is a simple fix; I was able to get it working by shimming `container.lookupProperty` similarly to how you have shimmed `escapeExpression`.  I'll open a PR shortly with a fix and additional tests.\r\n\r\nThanks!",
